The euro is accepted in <a href="/wiki/Campione_d%27Italia" title="Campione d'Italia">Campione d'Italia</a> but its official currency is the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_franc" title="Swiss franc">Swiss franc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></span></li>
            <li value="3"><span style="font-size:100%;">To call <a href="/wiki/Campione_d%27Italia" title="Campione d'Italia">Campione d'Italia</a>, it is necessary to use the Swiss code <a href="/w/index.php?title=%2B41&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="+41 (not yet started)">+41</a>.</span></li>
            <li value="4"><span style="font-size:100%;">The <a href="/wiki/.eu" class="mw-redirect" title=".eu">.eu</a> domain is also used, as it is shared with other <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states.</span></li> 
           </ol>

       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p><b>Italy</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> in south <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. Its official name is <b>Repubblica Italiana</b>. The Italian flag is green, white and red. Italy is a <a href="/wiki/Democratic" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic">democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> and is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EU_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU-7">[7]</a></sup> Its President is <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Mattarella" title="Sergio Mattarella">Sergio Mattarella</a> and its Prime Minister is <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Conte" title="Giuseppe Conte">Giuseppe Conte</a>. Italy is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a>, as it has the eighth largest <a href="/wiki/Gross_Domestic_Product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross Domestic Product">Gross Domestic Product</a> in the world. </p>
      <p>Before 1861, it was made up of smaller kingdoms and city-states. Italy has become famous for its wine, as well as its food. Some foods are different between regions. Famous dishes include various types of <a href="/wiki/Pasta" title="Pasta">pasta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pizza" title="Pizza">pizza</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grape</a>s. <a href="/wiki/Olive_(fruit)" title="Olive (fruit)">Olive</a>s are much used. </p>
      <p>The country's capital, <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, is one of the most famous cities in the world, as it was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. Other famous cities in Italy include, <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palermo" title="Palermo">Palermo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>. </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: Geography">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Italian_Peninsula" title="Italian Peninsula">Italian Peninsula</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_Italy_in_March_2003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Satellite_image_of_Italy_in_March_2003.jpg/170px-Satellite_image_of_Italy_in_March_2003.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Satellite_image_of_Italy_in_March_2003.jpg/255px-Satellite_image_of_Italy_in_March_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Satellite_image_of_Italy_in_March_2003.jpg/340px-Satellite_image_of_Italy_in_March_2003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4800" data-file-height="6000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_Italy_in_March_2003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Satellite_(artificial)" title="Satellite (artificial)">Satellite</a> image of Italy
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Italy is a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a>, meaning it is encompassed by the sea on all of its sides apart from one side of the country (its north side). Northern Italy is separated from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> a chain of mountains. <a href="/wiki/Mont_Blanc" title="Mont Blanc">Mont Blanc</a> (<i>Monte Bianco</i> in Italian or white mountain in English), the highest mountain in western <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> belongs to this chain. The second important chain of mountains in Italy is the <a href="/wiki/Apennines" class="mw-redirect" title="Apennines">Apennines</a> (<i>Appennini</i> in Italian), which are in central and southern Italy. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Capital_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (city)">capital</a> of Italy is Rome where the Roman Empire started. Other cities in Italy are <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palermo" title="Palermo">Palermo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>. The country has a number of islands, the biggest of which are <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-11">[11]</a></sup> which can be reached by ship or <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a>. It shares maritime borders with <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> to the south. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Po_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Po River">Po River</a> is the longest river in Italy. It flows through 5 cities: Torino, Piacenza, Cremona Ferrara and Rovigo.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tiber_River" title="Tiber River">Tiber River</a> runs through the city of <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>. </p>
      <p>Northern Italy has some of the biggest lakes in the country, such as <a href="/wiki/Lake_Garda" title="Lake Garda">Lake Garda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Como" title="Lake Como">Lake Como</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Maggiore" title="Lake Maggiore">Lake Maggiore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Iseo" title="Lake Iseo">Lake Iseo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Because it is surrounded by the sea, Italy has many <a href="/wiki/Kilometer" class="mw-redirect" title="Kilometer">kilometers</a> of <a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">coast</a>, which brings <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourists</a> from all over the world.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Tourists also come to see Italy's <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">historical</a> places.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Two very small separate countries are located within Italy. They are <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, which is surrounded by part of Northern Italy, and the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>, which is inside Rome. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People_and_culture">People and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: People and culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: People and culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_self.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Leonardo_self.jpg/220px-Leonardo_self.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="345" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Leonardo_self.jpg/330px-Leonardo_self.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Leonardo_self.jpg 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="659"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_self.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>People from Italy are called Italians. Even if an Italian were to leave Italy, it is possible that their descendants could also claim Italian <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizenship</a> due to Italian nationality law relying mostly on <i>ius sanguinis</i> or "right of blood" in Latin.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Nearly all the Italians are <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christians</a>, and most of these are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholics</a>, which is based in the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> and home to its leader, the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Leonardo da Vinci is a famous artist, he is the creator of the <a href="/wiki/Mona_Lisa" title="Mona Lisa">Mona Lisa</a> which is now in the louvre Paris. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> of Italy is a little over 60 million.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> About 2.7 million of them live in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> and 1.3 million in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> As of 31 December 2015, over 5 million foreigners were living in Italy, which is 8.3% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The official language of Italy is <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> and in some small areas German, Slovenian or French. People also speak <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a> of Italian such as Sicilian and Sardinian. There are many different dialects spoken in Italy. They vary between regions and, in some cases, also between provinces. </p>
      <p>The people of Italy are mostly <a href="/wiki/Descendant" class="mw-disambig" title="Descendant">descendant</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">ancient Romans</a>. </p>
      <p>Italy is home to more <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> than any other nation in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> These sites are culturally important and valued according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>. About 60% of the works of <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a> of the world are in Italy. Italy is also a big <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> producer. In 2005 it made over 5 million tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Economy">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Economy">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Italy has a modern social welfare system. The labor market enjoys relative strength, with many foreigners, especially from <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, working in Italy where the wages are much higher. But it could have been much more workers on the labor market because men and women already retired in the age of 57 and the unemployment rate is relatively high at 8.2 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Italy's modern society has been built up through loans and now the country has a catastrophic high debt of €1.9trn or 120 percent of the country's total GDP. And the government cannot pay back the loans during the time period the EU wish.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Religion">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: Religion">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Most people in Italy are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholics</a>, but the Catholic Church is no longer officially the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>. 87.8% of the people said they were Roman Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Only about a third said they were active members (36.8%). There are also other Christian groups in Italy, more than 700,000 <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christians</a>. 180,000 of them belong to the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>550,000 are <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelicals</a> (0.8%). 235,685 <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (0.4%),<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> 30,000 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Waldensian&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Waldensian (not yet started)">Waldensians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> 25,000 <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventist">Seventh-day Adventists</a>, 22,000 <a href="/wiki/Mormon" class="mw-redirect" title="Mormon">Mormons</a>, 20,000 <a href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">Baptists</a>, 7,000 <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutherans</a>, 4,000 <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The country's oldest religious minority is the <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish</a> community. It has roughly 45,000 people. It is no longer the largest non-Christian group. </p>
      <p> About 825,000 <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> live in Italy. Most of them immigrated.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> (1.4% of the total population) Only 50,000 are <a href="/w/index.php?title=Italian_nationality_law&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Italian nationality law (not yet started)">Italian citizens</a>. In addition, there are 50,000 <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> 70,000 <a href="/wiki/Sikh" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikh">Sikh</a><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> and 70,000 <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a> in Italy.</p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gondola-Venice-Italy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Gondola-Venice-Italy.jpg/220px-Gondola-Venice-Italy.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Gondola-Venice-Italy.jpg/330px-Gondola-Venice-Italy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Gondola-Venice-Italy.jpg/440px-Gondola-Venice-Italy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048"></a>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Food">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Food">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>During the celebration of <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Epiphany</a>, it's traditional to eat a special cake called 'Rosca de Reyes' Three Kings Cake. A figure of Baby Jesus is hidden inside the cake. Whoever has the baby Jesus in their piece of cake is the 'Godparent' of Jesus for that year. Famous Italian foods include pasta or pizza. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_cities">Major cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Major cities">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: Major cities">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Regions">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Regions">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Italy is <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/divide" class="extiw" title="wikt:divide">divided</a> into 20 Regions (<i>Regioni</i> in Italian) and every Region is divided into <a href="/w/index.php?title=Provinces_of_Itally&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Provinces of Itally (not yet started)">Provinces</a>. </p>
      <p>There are 20 Regions. 5 of them have a special status, they are called <i>autonomous</i>. This means that they can make certain local laws more easily. These regions are marked with an <a href="/wiki/Asterisk" title="Asterisk">asterisk</a> (*) below. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Politics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Politics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Obelisk_of_montecitorio_arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Obelisk_of_montecitorio_arp.jpg/170px-Obelisk_of_montecitorio_arp.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Obelisk_of_montecitorio_arp.jpg/255px-Obelisk_of_montecitorio_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Obelisk_of_montecitorio_arp.jpg/340px-Obelisk_of_montecitorio_arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1588" data-file-height="2119"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Obelisk_of_montecitorio_arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Italian_Chamber_of_Deputies" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Chamber of Deputies">Chamber of Deputies</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">Head of State</a> is <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Mattarella" title="Sergio Mattarella">Sergio Mattarella</a>, whose task began in February 2015. Mattarella is currently the President of the Italian Republic. The first president was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enrico_De_Nicola&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Enrico De Nicola (not yet started)">Enrico De Nicola</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">Head of Government</a> is <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Gentiloni" title="Paolo Gentiloni">Paolo Gentiloni</a>, who became <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a> on December 12, 2016, succeeding <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>. Renzi was previously the <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">Mayor</a> of <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a> and is Italy's youngest-ever <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a>, at age 39 when taking office. </p>
      <p>Italy was one of the first members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and in 2002 along with 11 other European countries, it changed to using the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> as its official <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a>. Before this, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Italian_lira&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Italian lira (not yet started)">Italian lira</a> had been used since 1861. </p>
      <p>Anyone who wants to be President of Italy must have Italian citizenship, be at least 50 years old, and must be able to hold political and <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights" title="Civil rights">civil rights</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-notice" role="presentation" style="CSS value">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wiki letter w.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/60px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/80px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="44"></a>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colosseum_in_Rome,_Italy_-_April_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Colosseum_in_Rome%2C_Italy_-_April_2007.jpg/220px-Colosseum_in_Rome%2C_Italy_-_April_2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Colosseum_in_Rome%2C_Italy_-_April_2007.jpg/330px-Colosseum_in_Rome%2C_Italy_-_April_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Colosseum_in_Rome%2C_Italy_-_April_2007.jpg/440px-Colosseum_in_Rome%2C_Italy_-_April_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4827" data-file-height="2833"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colosseum_in_Rome,_Italy_-_April_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Colosseum" title="Colosseum">Colosseum</a> in Rome. Its original name is Flavian Amphitheatre, being built under the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Flavian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Flavian dynasty (not yet started)">Flavian dynasty</a>, an imperial Family of the Ancient Rome.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Leaning_tower_of_pisa_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Leaning_tower_of_pisa_2.jpg/220px-Leaning_tower_of_pisa_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Leaning_tower_of_pisa_2.jpg/330px-Leaning_tower_of_pisa_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Leaning_tower_of_pisa_2.jpg/440px-Leaning_tower_of_pisa_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="555" data-file-height="740"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Leaning_tower_of_pisa_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Leaning_Tower_of_Pisa" title="Leaning Tower of Pisa">Leaning Tower of Pisa</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Before 1861, Italy was not a <a href="/wiki/State" title="State">state</a>. The area was made of a group of separate states, ruled by other countries (such as Austria, France, and Spain). In the 1850s the <a href="/wiki/Earl" title="Earl">Earl</a> of <a href="/wiki/Camillo_Benso,_Count_of_Cavour" title="Camillo Benso, Count of Cavour">Camillo Benso, Count of Cavour</a> was the Head of Government of the "State of Sardinia". He talked to the Austrians in Lombardy and Veneto and said they should create a Northern Italian state. This happened, but other Central and Southern Italian states also joined Piedmont to create a bigger state. </p>
      <p>In 1860, <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a> took control of Sicily, creating the Kingdom of Italy in 1861.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Victor_Emmanuel_II_of_Italy" title="Victor Emmanuel II of Italy">Victor Emmanuel II</a> was made the king. But in 1861, Latium and Veneto were still not part of Italy, because they were ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> and Austrian Empire. </p>
      <p>Veneto was made part of Italy in 1866 after a war with Austria, and Italian soldiers won Latium in 1870. That was when they took away the Pope's power. The Pope, who was angry, said that he was a prisoner to keep <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> people from being active in politics. That was the year of <a href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a>. </p>
      <p>Italy participated in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Ally" class="mw-redirect" title="Ally">ally</a> of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, and Russia against the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>. Almost all of Italy's fighting was on the Eastern <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">border</a>, near Austria. After the "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Caporetto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Caporetto (not yet started)">Caporetto</a> defeat", Italy thought they would lose the war. But, in 1918, the Central Powers <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/surrender" class="extiw" title="wikt:surrender">surrendered</a>, and Italy gained the Trentino-South Tyrol, which once was owned by Austria. </p>
      <p>In 1922, a new Italian government started. It was ruled by <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>, the leader of <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">Fascism</a> in Italy. He became <a href="/wiki/Head_of_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Head of Government">Head of Government</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dictator" title="Dictator">dictator</a>, calling himself "duce" - which means "<a href="/wiki/Leader" title="Leader">leader</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>. He became friends with German dictator <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a>, and Italy became the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a> and entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> together in 1940 against France, Great Britain, and later the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. During the war, Italy controlled most of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>. </p>
      <p>On July 25, 1943, Mussolini was removed by the Great Council of Fascism, and, on September 8, 1943, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Badoglio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Badoglio (not yet started)">Badoglio</a> said that the war as an ally of Germany was ended. Italy started fighting as an ally of France and the UK, but Italian soldiers did not know whom to shoot. In Northern Italy, a <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/movement" class="extiw" title="wikt:movement">movement</a> called <a href="/wiki/Italian_resistance_movement" title="Italian resistance movement">Resistenza</a> started to fight against the German <a href="/wiki/Invasion" title="Invasion">invaders</a>. </p>
      <p>Mussolini tried to make a small Northern Italian <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a> state, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Sal%C3%B2&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Republic of Salò (not yet started)">Republic of Salò</a>, but it failed. On <a href="/wiki/April_25" title="April 25">April 25</a>, 1945, Italy became free. The state became a republic on <a href="/wiki/June_2" title="June 2">June 2</a>, 1946, and, for the first time, women were able to vote. Italian people ended the Savoia <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">dynasty</a> and adopted a republic government. </p>
      <p>In February 1947, Italy signed a peace treaty with the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> losing all the colonies and some territorial areas: (<a href="/wiki/Istria" title="Istria">Istria</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatia</a>). </p>
      <p>Since then Italy has joined <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and the European Community (as a founding member), becoming one of the seven biggest industrial economies in the world. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Transportation">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Italy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Transportation">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rom_Fiumicino_Airport_2008_by-RaBoe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rom_Fiumicino_Airport_2008_by-RaBoe.jpg/220px-Rom_Fiumicino_Airport_2008_by-RaBoe.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="94" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rom_Fiumicino_Airport_2008_by-RaBoe.jpg/330px-Rom_Fiumicino_Airport_2008_by-RaBoe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rom_Fiumicino_Airport_2008_by-RaBoe.jpg/440px-Rom_Fiumicino_Airport_2008_by-RaBoe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="342"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rom_Fiumicino_Airport_2008_by-RaBoe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci-Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leonardo da Vinci-Fiumicino Airport (not yet started)">Rome-Fiumicino Airport</a> was the <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe (not yet started)">sixth busiest airport</a> in Europe in 2008.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">railway</a> <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/network#Noun" class="extiw" title="wikt:network">network</a> in Italy totals 16,627 kilometres (10,332&nbsp;mi), the 17th longest in the world. High speed trains include <a href="/w/index.php?title=ElettroTreno&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ElettroTreno (not yet started)">ETR</a>-class trains which travel at 300&nbsp;km/h (190&nbsp;mph). </p>
